<p>The <b>Angola national football team</b>, nicknamed <i>Palancas Negras (<a href="/wiki/Giant_sable_antelope" title="Giant sable antelope">Giant sable antelopes</a>)</i>, represents <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> in international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Football_Federation" title="Angolan Football Federation">Angolan Football Federation</a>, the governing body of <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> in the country. 
</p><p>Angola reached its highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_ranking" title="FIFA ranking">FIFA ranking</a>, 45th place, in July 2000. Their greatest accomplishment was qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, as this was their first appearance on the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals stage.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Angola played their first game against <a href="/wiki/Congo_national_football_team" title="Congo national football team">Congo</a> on 8 February 1976, losing 3–2. On 26 June 1977, <a href="/wiki/Cuba_national_football_team" title="Cuba national football team">Cuba</a> became Angola's first non-African opponent when the two countries met in Angola, with Angola winning 1-0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Angola entered World Cup qualifying for the first time in the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CAF)" title="1986 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)">1986 qualifying competition</a>. Angola defeated <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a> on penalties in the first round before narrowly losing to <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> 3-2 on aggregate in the second round.
</p><p>Angola qualified for their first <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996_African_Nations_Cup" title="1996 African Nations Cup">1996</a>. They were drawn in Group A with <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a>. They lost their first two games to Egypt and South Africa, but managed a 3–3 draw against Cameroon. They finished bottom of the group and did not reach the second round. Angola then qualified for their second successive African Cup of Nations in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1998_African_Nations_Cup" title="1998 African Nations Cup">1998</a>, but again failed to reach the second round, drawing 0–0 with South Africa and 3–3 with <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_football_team" title="Namibia national football team">Namibia</a>, and losing 5–2 to <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast</a>.
</p><p>After missing the last 3 tournaments, they qualified for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_African_Nations_Cup" title="2006 African Nations Cup">2006 African Nations Cup</a>. They recorded their first African Cup of Nations win against <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team" title="Togo national football team">Togo</a>, winning 3–2, two goals coming from <a href="/wiki/Fl%C3%A1vio_Amado" title="Flávio Amado">Flávio</a> and the other coming from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norberto_Mulenessa_Maurito" title="Norberto Mulenessa Maurito">Maurito</a>. They also drew 0–0 against <a href="/wiki/DR_Congo_national_football_team" title="DR Congo national football team">Congo DR</a> and lost 3–1 against Cameroon. Angola's best performance then came in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_African_Nations_Cup" title="2008 African Nations Cup">2008 African Nations Cup</a>. They were drawn in Group D with <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a>. They drew 1–1 and 0–0 with South Africa and Tunisia, then defeated Senegal 3–1, two goals coming from <a href="/wiki/Manucho" title="Manucho">Manucho</a>. In the quarter-finals they were beaten by eventual winners <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a> 2–1, but Manucho scored again, finishing with four goals in total.
</p><p>Angola also won the <a href="/wiki/COSAFA_Cup" title="COSAFA Cup">COSAFA Cup</a> in 1999, 2001 and 2004.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_FIFA_World_Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2006 FIFA World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Angola qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> after only losing one game in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CAF_Group_4" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Group 4">qualifiers</a> ahead of favourites <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a>.
</p><p>When picking the squad, Gonçalves sought advice from <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>, whose wife was born in Angola. Angola's <i>Golden Generation</i> saw players like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akw%C3%A1_(footballer)" title="Akwá (footballer)">Akwá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Ricardo" title="João Ricardo">João Ricardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Figueiredo" title="Paulo Figueiredo">Paulo Figueiredo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamba_(footballer)" title="Jamba (footballer)">Jamba</a> selected to go to the World Cup. Angola played six warm-up games against <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_national_football_team" title="Mauritius national football team">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_national_football_team" title="Lesotho national football team">Lesotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA</a>.
</p><p>Angola played their first World Cup finals game against the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portuguese side</a>, who won the match 1–0, the only goal coming from <a href="/wiki/Pauleta" title="Pauleta">Pauleta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> There was a very friendly environment in and around the stadium during this match because of the links and friendship between the countries of <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. Angola drew 0–0 in their second game with <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a>, and still had a chance of qualifying for the second round had they beaten <a href="/wiki/Iran_national_football_team" title="Iran national football team">Iran</a> in their final group game, but the match finished 1–1 after goals by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flavio_Amado" title="Flavio Amado">Flávio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sohrab_Bakhtiarizadeh" title="Sohrab Bakhtiarizadeh">Sohrab Bakhtiarizadeh</a>. Angola were eliminated from the tournament only losing one game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1490" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg/200px-Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg/300px-Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg/400px-Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fans_of_the_Angolan_national_football_team_in_Cologne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fans of the Angolan national football team in Cologne, Germany.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_World_Cup_failure">2010 World Cup failure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2010 World Cup failure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, many of Angola's most experienced players such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akw%C3%A1_(footballer)" title="Akwá (footballer)">Akwá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Ricardo" title="João Ricardo">João Ricardo</a> retired from the international game, but the expectation was still high for the team to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. The team had a bye through the first round of qualification and in the second round they were drawn in Group 3 along with <a href="/wiki/Benin_national_football_team" title="Benin national football team">Benin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_football_team" title="Uganda national football team">Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niger_national_football_team" title="Niger national football team">Niger</a>. Despite winning their first two matches, Angola failed to proceed to the third round, missing out by two points.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations">2010 Africa Cup of Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2010 Africa Cup of Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As hosts of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">2010 Africa Cup of Nations</a>, Angola were seeded in Group A along with <a href="/wiki/Mali_national_football_team" title="Mali national football team">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malawi_national_football_team" title="Malawi national football team">Malawi</a>. Coached by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9" title="Manuel José">Manuel José</a>, in their first game they drew 4–4 with Mali, after letting a 4–0 lead slip in the last 11 minutes (including three goals in stoppage time). They recovered from this by beating Malawi 2–0 in the second match, and topped the group by drawing 0–0 with Algeria. They were knocked out in the quarter final after a 1–0 defeat by eventual finalists Ghana.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_(001).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg/250px-Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg/375px-Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg/500px-Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_%28001%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iran_vs._Angola_2014-05-30_(001).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Angola lining-up before a friendly match in 2014</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_records">Competition records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Competition records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup_record">World Cup record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World Cup record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Angola_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Angola at the FIFA World Cup">Angola at the FIFA World Cup</a></div>
<p>As of 2018, Angola has qualified once for a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>. Its first participation in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="FIFA World Cup qualification">World Cup qualifiers</a> was in <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CAF)" title="1986 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)">1986</a>, where they won in the first round, beating <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a> 4−3 on penalty kicks. They later lost in the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CAF)#Second_round" title="1986 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)">second round</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="1986 FIFA World Cup qualification">1986 World Cup qualifiers</a> to <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a>. Algeria went to the third round and qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.
</p><p>Angola's first participation in the World Cup was in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="vevent"><span class="summary" style="display:none"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Angola</a><span class="flagicon"> <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/23px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/35px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/45px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span> v <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/23px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/35px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_Botswana.svg/45px-Flag_of_Botswana.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Botswana_national_football_team" title="Botswana national football team">Botswana</a></span></span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following players have been selected for the <a href="/wiki/2021_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_qualification_Group_D" title="2021 Africa Cup of Nations qualification Group D">2021 Africa Cup of Nations qualification</a> against <a href="/wiki/Gambia_national_football_team" title="Gambia national football team">Gambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabon_national_football_team" title="Gabon national football team">Gabon</a> on 13 and 17 November 2019 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><br/>
<i>Caps and goals as of 17 November 2019 after the game against <a href="/wiki/Gabon_national_football_team" title="Gabon national football team">Gabon</a>.</i>
